Appendix D
Air Quality Data
JACKSON VALLEY QUARRY EXPANSION
Health Risk Assessment

Exposure levels of toxic air contaminants generated by the proposed quarry expansion were
estimated by conducting dispersion modeling of potential toxic air contaminant (TAC) sources at
the project site. TAC emission sources evaluated in this health risk assessment were based on
information contained in the Air Quality Section of this EIR, and they include: diesel particulate
matter (DPM) exhaust emissions from heavy duty equipment and haul trucks and fugitive dust
emissions of crystalline silica. The emissions from these sources were input to the USEPA
approved dispersion model AERMOD to calculate ambient air concentrations in the area
surrounding the project site. The output from AERMOD was then analyzed in accordance with
guidelines established by the California Office of Environmental Health Hazards Assessment
(OEHHA) to assess non-cancer risks and cancer risks.


Emissions
Fugitive dust emissions may contain crystalline silica due to the large amount of quartz present at
the project site. As a conservative analysis it was assumed that 40% of all fugitive dust 2.5
microns or less in diameter (PM2.5) would be respirable quartz dust (crystalline silica). This
estimate was based on estimates of crystalline silica present in materials found at the project site
(George Reed Inc., 2003).

DPM emissions from heavy duty equipment and haul trucks were based on emissions estimates
presented in the Air Quality Section of this EIR. It was assumed that all PM2.5 exhaust emissions
from off-road equipment and haul trucks would be DPM.


Model Inputs and Results
To determine the worst case exposure, receptors were modeled at ground level breathing height.
Five consecutive years of meteorological data from the Mather Air Force Base meteorological
station was used to prepare hourly surface files for use in AERMOD. Figure 1 presents a wind
rose of the area, and it represents the data used in the model.




Project Name                                   Chapter #-1                               ESA / Project No.
Type of document                                                                                     Date
                                       Preliminary - Subject to Revision
Chapter Title




                               Figure 1
                   Mather Air Force Base Wind Rose
                   (Wind Direction - Blowing From)




Project Name                     Chapter #-2                 ESA / Project No.
Type of document                                                         Date
                         Preliminary - Subject to Revision
                                                                                 Chapter or Section Title




Source and receptor elevations were derived from the Ione 7.5 minute digital elevation model.
These elevations were processed and imported using AERMAP, an accessory program to
AERMOD. Off-road equipment and haul truck emissions were modeled as a series of volume
sources. Fugitive dust emissions were modeled as a large area source.

Based on modeling results, annual average concentrations of DPM from existing operations were
estimated to be approximately 0.024 g/m3 at the maximum exposed residential receptor (located
approximately 315 feet north of the proposed expansion site). Annual average concentrations of
crystalline silica at the maximum exposed receptor from existing operations were estimated to be
approximately 0.416 g/m3.

Annual average concentrations of DPM at the maximum exposed resident under the proposed
expansion were estimated to be approximately 0.050 g/m3, which represents a 0.026 g/m3
increase from existing operations. Annual average crystalline silica concentrations were estimated
to be approximately 1.012 g/m3; this represents an increase of approximately 0.596 g/m3 above
existing operations.


Health Risks
Cancer risk is defined as the probability of developing cancer from exposure to carcinogenic
substances over a lifetime. Cancer risk is expressed as increased chances in one million of
contracting cancer, and it can incorporate more than one exposure pathway (i.e., inhalation,
dermal contact, ingestion of contaminated soil, and infant ingestion of breast milk due to the
mother's cumulative exposure). Overall cancer risks are determined by summing the individual
risk for each pathway and for each TAC. OEHHA has identified DPM as a carcinogen.

Non-cancer adverse health risk, both for acute (short-term) and chronic (long-term) risk, is
measured against a hazard index, which is defined as the ratio of the predicted incremental
exposure concentration from the proposed project to a published reference exposure level (REL)
that could cause adverse health effects, which are established by OEHHA. The ratio (referred to
as the Hazard Quotient) of each non-carcinogenic substance that affects a certain organ system is
added to produce an overall Hazard Index for that organ system. Overall Hazard Indices are
calculated for each organ system. DPM and crystalline silica have both been identified as having
chronic health impacts to the respiratory system.

Cancer Risk
The maximum incremental cancer risk from exposure to DPM was calculated following the
guidelines established by California Office of Environmental Health Hazard Assessment
(OEHHA, 2003). The equation used to determine exposure to DPM through inhalation is
demonstrated below:

           Dose-inh         = Cair * {DBR} * A * EF * ED * 10-6
                                           AT
           Where:


Project Name                                  Chapter #-3                                ESA / Project No.
Type of document                                                                                     Date
                                      Preliminary - Subject to Revision
Chapter Title




                   Dose-inh   = Dose of the toxic substance through inhalation in milligrams per
                                kilogram of body weight per day (mg/kg-day)
                   10-6       = Micrograms to milligrams conversion, Liters to cubic meters
                                conversion
                   Cair       = Concentration in air (g/m3)
                   {DBR}      = Daily breathing rate (L/kg body weight  day)
                   A          = Inhalation absorption factor
                   EF         = Exposure frequency (days/year)
                   ED         = Exposure duration (years)
                   AT         = Averaging time period over which exposure is averaged in days
                                (25,550 days for a 70 year cancer risk)


Per OEHHA Guidelines, the 80th percentile adult breathing rate of 302 L/kg-day was used to
determine cancer risks from exposure to DPM during expanded operations. The exposure
frequency was assumed to be 350 days per year. According to the project description, the
proposed expansion would operate for a minimum of 25 years. Therefore, risk was evaluated
assuming both a 30 and 70-year exposure duration; the 30-year exposure duration represents the
more likely scenario whereas the 70-year exposure provides a worst case estimate of potential
cancer risk assuming the expanded quarry operates for 70-years. The modeled increase in DPM
concentration discussed previously was used to represent the concentration of DPM in the air.
The inhalation absorption factor was assumed to be 1.

To determine incremental cancer risk the estimated dose through inhalation was multiplied by
cancer potency slope factor for DPM, 1.1 (mg/kg-day)-1. As shown below, assuming the quarry
would only operate for 30 years, the maximum incremental cancer risk to sensitive receptors in
the project area would be approximately 3.6 in one million. This incremental level is below the
CEQA Significance Threshold of 10 in one million.

           Dose-inhalation    = 0.026 g/m3 * 302 L/kg-day * 1 *350 days/year * 30 years *10-6
                                                   (25,550 days)
                              = 3.23 * 10-6
           Cancer Risk        = 3.23 * 10-6 mg/kg-day * 1.1 (mg/kg-day)-1
                              = 3.55 * 10-6
                              ~ 3.6 in one million

Assuming that the quarry would operate for 70-years, the maximum incremental cancer risk from
expanded operations would be approximately 8.3 in one million. This incremental level is also
below the CEQA Significance Threshold of 10 in one million.

           Dose-inhalation    = 0.026 g/m3 * 302 L/kg-day * 1 *350 days/year * 70 years *10-6
                                                  (25,550 days)
                                          -6
                              = 7.53 * 10
           Cancer Risk        = 7.53 * 10-6 mg/kg-day * 1.1 (mg/kg-day)-1
                              = 8.28 * 10-6



Project Name                                   Chapter #-4                              ESA / Project No.
Type of document                                                                                    Date
                                       Preliminary - Subject to Revision
                                                                              Chapter or Section Title




                           ~ 8.3 in one million



Non-Cancer Risks
OEHHA has assigned diesel exhaust a chronic REL of 5.0 g/m3 and crystalline silica a chronic
REL of 3.0 g/m3. These RELs represent the levels at which exposure may result in adverse
health effects to the respiratory system. As discussed above, the proposed expansion would
increase concentrations of DPM by 0.026 g/m3 at the maximum exposed resident. Therefore, the
chronic hazard quotient for exposure to DPM would be approximately 0.005. Crystalline silica
concentrations would increase by approximately 0.596 g/m3, resulting in a hazard quotient of
approximately 0.2. Combined, the chronic hazard index from exposure to TACs generated during
operation of the proposed expansion would be approximately 0.205 for the respiratory system.
The predicted Hazard Index is below the CEQA Significance Threshold of 1.0.



References

George Reed Inc., 2003. Jackson Valley Quarry  Geologic Investigation  Asbestos &
       Ultramafic Rocks, submitted by D.E. Deem R.G., April 2, 2003.

Office of Environmental Health Hazards Assessment (OEHHA), 2003. The Air Toxics Hot Spots
        Program Guidance Manual for Preparation of Health Risk Assessments, available online
        at: http://www.oehha.org/air/hot_spots/pdf/HRAguidefinal.pdf, accessed April 29, 2008.
